'''''The Dr. Oz Show''''' is an American [[daytime television]] talk show. Each episode has segments on health, wellness and medical information, sometimes including [[true crime]] stories and celebrity interviews.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/live-feed/dr-oz-show-renewed-season-901022 |title='The Dr. Oz Show' Renewed for Season 10 |website=The Hollywood Reporter |language=en |access-date=2018-12-31}}</ref> It is co-produced by Oprah Winfrey's [[Harpo Productions]] and distributed by [[Sony Pictures Television]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Episodes: ''The Dr. Oz Show''|url=http://www.doctoroz.com/episode/oz-celebrates-his-1000th-show-hugh-jackman|work=TV Guide|accessdate=November 29, 2015}}</ref>

The series is hosted by [[Mehmet Oz]] and debuted in 2009. ''The Dr. Oz Show'' has received nine [[Daytime Emmy Award]]s during its run, five for Outstanding Informative Talk Show and four for Outstanding Informative Talk Show Host, as well as criticism for some of its subject matter.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://deadline.com/2019/03/daytime-emmys-nominations-2019-days-of-our-lives-general-hospital-young-and-the-restless-1202579062/ |title=Daytime Emmy Nominations: 'Days Of Our Lives' Leads Programs & CBS Tops Networks |last=Pedersen |first=Erik |date=2019-03-20 |website=Deadline |language=en |access-date=2019-04-20}}</ref>

In April 2018, ''The Dr. Oz Show'' was renewed for seasons 11 and 12, through 2020–21 season.<ref name=broadcastingcable/><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://tvseriesfinale.com/tv-show/the-dr-oz-show-renewed-for-seasons-11-and-12-through-2020-21-season/|title=The Dr. Oz Show: Renewed for Seasons 11 and 12, Through 2020-21 Season|date=2018-04-30|website=canceled TV shows - TV Series Finale|language=en-US|access-date=2019-08-29}}</ref> In September 2020, ''The Dr. Oz Show'' was renewed for seasons 13 and 14, through 2022–23 season.<ref name="Seasons 13 & 14 Renewed"/>

==History==
[[File:Michelle Obama and Dr. Mehmet Oz learn a dance routine during a taping of the “Dr. Oz Show”, 2013.jpg|thumb|[[Michelle Obama]] and [[Mehmet Oz]] dance routine from a 2013 episode of ''The Dr. Oz Show'']]
In 2009, Winfrey offered to produce a syndicated series featuring Mehmet Oz through her company, Harpo Productions.<ref name=newyorker/> ''The Dr. Oz Show'' debuted September 14, 2009. It received [[Daytime Emmy]] nominations for Outstanding Talk Show Informative and Outstanding Talk Show Informative Host in 2010, winning the latter.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://deadline.com/2010/06/2010-daytime-emmy-winners-as-the-world-turns-bold-beautiful-cash-cab-and-dr-oz-49888/ |title=2010 Daytime Emmy Winners: 'As The World Turns', 'Bold & Beautiful', 'Young & Restless', 'General Hospital', 'Cash Cab', 'Ellen', 'Dr Oz', And 'The Doctors' |last=Finke |first=Nikki  |date=2010-06-28 |website=Deadline |language=en |access-date=2018-12-31}}</ref>

For the first four seasons, shows were recorded in Studio 6A at [[NBC Studios (New York City)|NBC Studios]] in New York,<ref name="myfoxny.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.myfoxny.com/subindex/health/Dr_Oz |title=Dr. Oz&nbsp;— New York News &#124; NYC Breaking News |publisher=Myfoxny.com |date= |accessdate=November 26, 2012}}</ref> but vacated [[Rockefeller Center]] after NBC reclaimed the space for its ''[[Late Night (NBC)|Late Night]]'' franchise.<ref>{{cite web|last=Bond|first=Paul|title=NBC Dumps $25 Million Jimmy Fallon NYC 'Tonight Show' Studio|url=http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/jimmy-fallon-tonight-show-nbc-518867|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|accessdate=September 4, 2013|date=May 7, 2013}}</ref> Beginning with season five, ''The Dr. Oz Show'' is filmed in the ABC Television Center East on the [[Upper West Side]] of [[Manhattan]].<ref>[http://www.doctoroz.com/get-show-tickets Get Show Tickets! | The Dr. Oz Show<!-- Bot generated title -->]</ref>

In April 2018, Sony Pictures Television renewed ''The Dr. Oz Show'' for seasons 11 and 12, taking it through 2020–21.<ref name=broadcastingcable>{{Cite web |url=https://www.broadcastingcable.com/news/dr-oz-live-long-healthy-life-syndication |title='Dr. Oz' to Live Long, Healthy Life in Syndication |last=Albiniak |first=Paige |website=Broadcasting & Cable |language=en-us |access-date=2018-12-31}}</ref>

In March 2020, in-studio production was shut down after a staffer experienced "subtle" symptoms and tested positive for [[COVID-19]]. Episodes began filming at Oz's home afterward. The show announced that it would return to studio tapings for its season premiere on September 14, 2020 with limited crew members and without a live audience.<ref>{{Cite web |title=The Dr. Oz Show Resumes Production in Studio amid COVID-19 Pandemic |url=https://people.com/tv/dr-oz-show-resumes-production-in-studio/ |access-date=2020-09-09 |website=PEOPLE.com |language=EN}}</ref>

In September 2020, ''The Dr. Oz Show'' was renewed for seasons 13 and 14, through 2022–23.<ref name="Seasons 13 & 14 Renewed">{{Cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2020/09/dr-oz-renewed-two-seasons-2023-1234575701/|title='The Dr. Oz Show' Renewed For Seasons 13 & 14 Ahead Of Today's Fall Premiere|date=2020-09-14|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|language=en-US|access-date=2020-09-15}}</ref>

==Reception==
{{further|Medical claims on The Dr. Oz Show}}
According to ''[[The New Yorker]]'', the series is "among the most highly rated daily television programs" in the United States.<ref name=newyorker>{{Cite web |url=https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2013/02/04/the-operator |title=The Operator |last=Specter |first=Michael |date=2013-01-28 |website=The New Yorker |language=en |access-date=2018-12-31}}</ref> It consistently scores ratings with daytime television's primary demographic of women from ages 25–54.<ref name=broadcastingcable/> During the 2016 season, ''The Dr. Oz Show'' averaged a 1.4 Nielsen household rating in live-plus-same day numbers.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://variety.com/2016/tv/news/dr-oz-renewed-1201791854/ |title='Dr. Oz' Renewed Through 2018-19 Season |last=Holloway |first=Daniel  |date=2016-06-09 |website=Variety |language=en |access-date=2018-12-31}}</ref> It had a 1.2 Nielsen household rating in 2017 and a 1.1 rating during the 2018 season.<ref name=broadcastingcable/>

Over the course of its run, ''The Dr. Oz Show'' and other similar medical talk shows have been criticized for featuring subject matter that is not supported by published studies. The ''[[British Medical Journal]]'' found that more than half of the recommendations on these shows contradicted medical research.<ref>{{Cite journal |title=Televised medical talk shows—what they recommend and the evidence to support their recommendations: a prospective observational study |last1=Allan |first1=G. Michael |last2=Vandermeer |first2=Ben |date=2014-12-17 |journal=BMJ |volume=349 |pages=g7346 |language=en |doi=10.1136/bmj.g7346 |pmid=25520234 |last3=Campbell-Scherer |first3=Denise |last4=Banh |first4=Hoan Linh |last5=Lindblad |first5=Adrienne J. |last6=Garrison |first6=Scott |last7=Turgeon |first7=Ricky D. |last8=Finley |first8=Caitlin |last9=Cotton |first9=Candra|pmc=4269523 |doi-access=free }}</ref> Producers for the show have stated that the series gives viewers "the most information and the greatest number of tools they can use to make their own choices."<ref name=newyorker/>
